## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

### Core Components:

1. **Filter Interfaces** - Define what filters can do (StreamDecoderFilter, StreamEncoderFilter, StreamFilter)

2. **Filter Factory Interfaces** - Define how filter chains are created (FilterChainFactory, FilterChainManager, FilterChainFactoryCallbacks)

3. **Filter Registry** - Enables plugin registration (NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory, UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory)

4. **Per-Request Execution Engine** - Handles filter chain execution for each request (FilterManager, ActiveStreamFilterBase, ActiveStreamDecoderFilter, ActiveStreamEncoderFilter)

6. **Filter Chain Creation** - Orchestrates filter chain instantiation (HttpConnectionManagerConfig, FilterChainUtility)

7. **Base Classes** - Provides reusable implementations (FactoryBase, DualFactoryBase)

The document provides a detailed narrative explaining how these components work together to enable Envoy's flexible HTTP filter extensibility, including support for dynamic filter loading via xDS and sequential filter execution with control flow based on status returns.

The HCM selects a route from its\\n441: ``RouteConfiguration`` at the start of HTTP filter chain execution. This is referred to as the\\n442: *cached route*. Filters may modify headers and cause a new route to be selected, by asking HCM to\\n443: clear the route cache and requesting HCM to reevaluate the route selection. The factory is aware of the filter\u2019s configuration and creates a new instance of the\\n249: filter for each connection or stream.\\n250: \\n251: In the case of our TLS listener configuration, the listener filter chain consists of the :ref:`TLS\\n252: inspector <config_listener_filters_tls_inspector>` filter\\n253: (``envoy.filters.listener.tls_inspector``).             "content": "438: \n439: When ``decodeHeaders()`` is invoked on the :ref:`router <arch_overview_http_routing>` filter, the\n440: route selection is finalized and a cluster is picked. The HCM selects a route from its\n441: ``RouteConfiguration`` at the start of HTTP filter chain execution. This is referred to as the\n442: *cached route*. Filters may modify headers and cause a new route to be selected, by asking HCM to\n443: clear the route cache and requesting HCM to reevaluate the route selection. Filters may also\n444: directly set this cached route selection via a ``setRoute`` callback. When the router filter is\n445: invoked, the route is finalized. The selected route\u2019s configuration will point at an upstream\n446: cluster name. The router filter then asks the ``ClusterManager`` for an HTTP :ref:`connection pool\n447: <arch_overview_conn_pool>` for the cluster. This involves load balancing and the connection pool,\n448: ",
            "endLine": 448,
            "startLine": 438

            "content": "242: \n243: 2. Listener filter chains and network filter chain matching\n244: ^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^^\n245: ",

            "startLine": 242
          },
          {
            "content": "245: \n246: The worker thread\u2019s *Listener* then creates and runs the :ref:`listener filter\n247: <arch_overview_listener_filters>` chain. Filter chains are created by applying each filter\u2019s *filter\n248: factory*. The factory is aware of the filter\u2019s configuration and creates a new instance of the\n249: filter for each connection or stream.\n250: \n251: In the case of our TLS listener configuration, the listener filter chain consists of the :ref:`TLS\n252: inspector <config_listener_filters_tls_inspector>` filter\n253: (``envoy.filters.listener.tls_inspector``). This filter examines the initial TLS handshake and\n254: extracts the server name (SNI). The SNI is then made available for filter chain matching. While the\n255: TLS inspector appears explicitly in the listener filter chain configuration, Envoy is also capable\n256: of inserting this automatically whenever there is a need for SNI (or ALPN) in a listener\u2019s filter\n257: chain.\n258: \n259: .. image:: /_static/lor-listener-filters.svg\n260:    :width: 80%\n261: ",

Interfaces (envoy/http/filter_factory.h)\\nThese interfaces define the contract for filter chain creation:\\n- `FilterChainFactory` - Called when a new HTTP stream is created to instantiate the filter chain\\n- `FilterChainManager` - Acts as the \\\"sink\\\" that receives filter factories and builds the filter chain\\n- `FilterChainFactoryCallbacks` - Provides methods like addStreamDecoderFilter(), addStreamEncoderFilter(), addAccessLogHandler() to register filters with the chain\\n- `FilterFactoryCb` - Typedef for the factory callback function that creates and registers filter instances\\n- interface for upstream HTTP filters\\n- These implement the Registry pattern allowing filter configurations to be looked up and instantiated\\n\\n## Per-Request Filter Chain Execution (source/common/http/filter_manager.h, filter_manager.cc)\\nThe core execution engine:\\n- `FilterManager` - Manages execution of the filter chain for a single request/response stream, implementing both decoder and encoder phases\\n- `DownstreamFilterManager` - Specialized FilterManager for downstream requests\\n- `ActiveStreamFilterBase` - Base for active filter wrappers that handle filter callbacks and state transitions\\n- `ActiveStreamDecoderFilter` - Wraps a decoder filter and manages its execution during decode phase\\n- `ActiveStreamEncoderFilter` - Wraps an encoder filter and manages its execution during encode phase\\n- The FilterManager iterates through decoder filters in sequence during request processing and encoder filters in reverse sequence during response FilterManagers\\n- Creates a new FilterManager for each HTTP stream\\n- Calls the FilterChainFactory when a new stream arrives to build the filter chain\\n\\n## Filter Chain Creation Flow (source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h, filter_chain_helper.cc, source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h, config.cc)\\nThe process of instantiating filter chains:\\n- HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain() is called\\n- This calls FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories() which applies each configured filter factory in order\\n- Each factory factories:\\n- `FactoryBase<ConfigProto, RouteSpecificConfigProto>` - Template base for downstream-only filters\\n- `DualFactoryBase<ConfigProto, RouteSpecificConfigProto>` - Template base for filters supporting both upstream and downstream contexts\\n- Provides default implementations of createFilterFactoryFromProto() methods\\n\\n## Dynamic Filter Configuration (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h)\\nSupport for dynamic filter configuration:\\n- `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` - Allows filter configuration to be updated at runtime via xDS without restarting\\n- Manages subscription to filter config updates\\n\\n## Helper Utilities (source/extensions/filters/http/common/pass_through_filter.h)\\n- `PassThroughFilter` - Convenient base class for filters that don't modify the stream data\\n- Provides default implementations of all filter methods that just continue the chain\\n\\nThis architecture enables Envoy's flexible HTTP filter extensibility where filters can be plugged in at configuration time, dynamically loaded via xDS, and executed in sequence with control over iteration flow based on status returns.\"\n}\n",

factories to the FilterChainManager\\n- `FilterChainHelper` - Template class that manages the complete filter chain creation process including dynamic filter loading\\n- When a new stream arrives, HttpConnectionManagerConfig::createFilterChain() is called\\n- This calls FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories() which applies each configured filter factory in order\\n- Each factory callback is applied via FilterChainManager::applyFilterFactoryCb()\\n\\n## Filter Factory Base Classes (source/extensions/filters/http/common/factory_base.h)\\nReusable implementations for filter factories:\\n- `FactoryBase<ConfigProto, RouteSpecificConfigProto>` - Template base for downstream-only filters\\n- `DualFactoryBase<ConfigProto, RouteSpecificConfigProto>` - Template base for filters supporting both upstream and downstream contexts\\n- Provides default implementations of createFilterFactoryFromProto() methods\\n\\n## Dynamic Filter Configuration (source/common/filter/config_discovery_impl.h)\\nSupport for dynamic filter configuration:\\n- `HttpDynamicFilterConfigProviderImpl` - Allows filter configuration to be updated at runtime via xDS without restarting\\n- Manages subscription to filter config updates\\n\\n## Helper Utilities (source/extensions/filters/http/common/pass_through_filter.h)\\n- `PassThroughFilter` - Convenient base class for filters that don't modify the stream data\\n- Provides default implementations of all filter methods that just continue the chain\\n\\nThis architecture enables Envoy's flexible HTTP filter extensibility where filters can be plugged in at configuration time, dynamically loaded via xDS, and executed in sequence with control over iteration flow based on status returns.\"\n}\n",
